Given the small dimensions (B=2, S=8, N=32, D=64, H=32), shared memory sizes: - MSA attn: `2*N*D + 2*(128/32)*N*head_dim` = 2*32*64 + 2*4*32*16 = 4096 + 4096 = 8192 floats = 32 KB. Good. - OPM: `2*S*D_msa + 2*S*H + H*H` = 2*8*64 + 2*8*32 + 32*32 = 1024 + 512 + 1024 = 2560 floats = 10 KB. Good. - TriMul: `2*N*D_pair + 2*N*H + H + D_pair` = 2*32*64 + 2*32*32 + 32 + 64 = 4096 + 2048 + 96 = 6240 floats = 24.375 KB. Good. All within 48KB shared memory. Let me verify the MSA attention kernel: - For each (B, S) block, 128 threads. - Loads N*D = 2048 floats to shared memory. 128 threads each load ~16 floats. - LayerNorm: threads 0..31 each process one row. N=32, so exactly 32 threads. Works. - Per-head attention: `warp_id = tid/32`. `num_heads=4`. `blockDim.x=128`, so 4 warps. Warp 0 handles head 0, warp 1 head 1, etc. - Lane = n (0..31). But N=32, so lane 0..31 maps to n 0..31. Perfect. - Each warp computes Q, K, V for its 32 rows. - Shared memory for K and V: `smem_k_base` starts at `smem + 2*N*D`. Size per warp = `N*head_dim` = 32*16 = 512 floats. Total for 4 warps = 2048 floats. - `smem_v_base` similar. Total = 4096 floats. So total SMEM = 2*2048 + 4096 = 8192 floats. OK. - Q @ K^T: each thread computes scores[m] for m=0..31. 32 scores per thread. Fine. - Softmax in registers. - Attn @ V. - Write to `smem_attn` at `n*D + h*head_dim + dh`. - Output linear + residual: each thread computes a few output elements. - `out_msa[(((b*S+s)*N)*D) + i] = msa_ptr[i] + acc;` - `msa_ptr[i]` is the original MSA value, `acc` is the output projection. - This seems correct. Wait, the output linear uses `smem_attn` which contains the attention output. The output linear is `self.out(out)` where `out` is shape `(B, S, N, D)`. So computing `acc = ob[d_out] + sum(smem_attn[n, d] * ow[d_out, d])` is correct because `ow` is `(D, D)`. One subtlety: in LayerNorm, we use `norm_w` and `norm_b`, which are shape `(D,)`. That's correct. For Q, K, V linear projections: - Reference: `q = self.q(x).view(B, S, N, h, d).permute(0, 1, 3, 2, 4)` - `self.q` is `nn.Linear(msa_dim, msa_dim)` with weight shape `(D, D)`. - Input `x` is `(B, S, N, D)`. Output is `(B, S, N, D)`. - Then reshaped to `(B, S, N, h, d)` and permuted to `(B, S, h, N, d)`. - In my kernel, for head `h` and row `n`, I compute: `sum_{d} x[n, d] * qw[h*head_dim + dh, d]`. - In PyTorch, `nn.Linear` does `y = x @ W^T + b`. So weight is `(D, D)`, and `W^T` is used. - Wait, in PyTorch `nn.Linear`, `weight` shape is `(out_features, in_features)`. So `self.q.weight` is `(D, D)`. - The operation is `q[x] = sum_d x[d] * weight[q, d]`. So the index order is `weight[out_d, in_d]`. - In my kernel, I do `const float* w = qw + (h * head_dim + dh) * D;` and `sum += smem_msa[n * D + d] * w[d];`. - This corresponds to `qw[out_d * D + in_d]`, which is correct for PyTorch's weight layout. - Then in the attention, Q is `(B, S, h, N, d)`, K is same. `q @ k.transpose(-1, -2)` corresponds to `sum_d q[n, d] * k[m, d]`. In my kernel: `dot += q_vec[dh] * my_k[m * head_dim + dh]`. Yes. - Output permutation: `(attn @ v).permute(0, 1, 3, 2, 4).reshape(B, S, N, D)`. `attn @ v` gives `(B, S, h, N, d)`. Permute to `(B, S, N, h, d)`, reshape to `(B, S, N, D)`. - In my kernel, `smem_attn[n * D + h * head_dim + dh]` stores the output in `(N, D)` order, which is `n * D + (h*head_dim + dh)`. So when reading for the output linear, `smem_attn[n * D + d]` is correct. - Output linear: `self.out(out)` where `out` is `(B, S, N, D)`. `self.out.weight` is `(D, D)`. My kernel computes `acc = ob[d_out] + sum_d smem_attn[n*D + d] * ow[d_out * D + d]`. This is correct. - Residual: `msa_repr + self.msa_attn(msa_repr)`. My kernel does `out_msa[...] = msa_ptr[i] + acc`. Correct. Outer Product Mean kernel: - For each (b, i, j) block. - Load MSA rows for `i` and `j`: `msa[b, :, i, :]` and `msa[b, :, j, :]`. Correct. - LayerNorm on both. Correct. - Compute `a` and `b` using `aw`, `ab`, `bw`, `bb`. Correct. - Outer product and sum over s: `sum_s a[s, h1] * b[s, h2]`. Correct. - Divide by S. Correct. - Linear projection: `self.out(outer.reshape(...))`. The reshape is `(B, N, N, H*H)`. `smem_outer` stores `H*H` elements. Output weight `ow` is `(D_pair, H*H)`. My kernel: `sum += smem_outer[h] * ow[d_out * (H*H) + h]`. Correct. - Residual add to pair: `pair_ptr[d_out] += sum`. Correct. TriMulOut kernel: - For each (b, i, j) block. - Load pair rows for `i` and `j`: `pair[b, i, :, :]` and `pair[b, j, :, :]`. Correct. - LayerNorm. Correct. - Compute `a[k, h] = pa(x_i[k]) * sigmoid(ga(x_i[k]))`. Correct. - Compute `b[k, h] = pb(x_j[k]) * sigmoid(gb(x_j[k]))`. Correct. - `o[h] = sum_k a[k, h] * b[k, h]`. Correct. The reference uses `torch.einsum("bikh,bjkh->bijh", a, b)`. For fixed `b, i, j`, it's `sum_k a[b,i,k,h] * b[b,j,k,h]`. Correct. - LayerNorm on `o`. Correct. - Output linear `self.out(norm_out(o))`. According to GCC man page: `-static-libstdc++` "When the g++ program is used to link a program or shared library, it will normally automatically link against libstdc++. If libstdc++ is available as a shared library, and the -static-libstdc++ option is not used, then this links against the shared version of libstdc++. That is normally fine. However, it is sometimes useful to freeze the version of libstdc++ used by the program without going all the way to a fully static link. The -static-libstdc++ option directs the g++ driver to link libstdc++ statically, without necessarily linking other libraries statically." So `g++ -shared -static-libstdc++` is valid and will link libstdc++ statically into the `.so`.
